<p dir="auto">MRS: We want to avoid module authors doing any explicit work</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: If default is</p>
<p dir="auto">DRR: (fill in point)</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: important to look at named imports and exports that don't change, vs. do</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: (spoke to fast for me to follow, but basically something about <code>module.exports = function() {}</code>?)</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: If we had a way to observe mutations, we may be able to track them, but it's not clear how we would do that</p>
<p dir="auto">YK: Empirically, most modules don't do mutation.</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: Module authors will get bugs reported to them that claim the issue is the new version of Node.</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: It's clear that all of the CJS and ESM lumped together will not work perfectly, but we can example things for use cases. Some may be automatic, others for tools, others impossible</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: We are trying to make these tradeoffs, but we want to make them in a sane manner; we want to look at whether which things would break the spec, or break what things on what end. We think users have a reasonable expectation to be able to do named imports from CJS modules. We will have to sacrifice some of the linking features in ESM, since Node's load cycle is a big block. We need to be able to break the tradeoff without violating the spec.</p>
<p dir="auto">YK: approach, get as close to the spec as possible, and come back to the committee with concrete points that need to be fixed.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: [Hoistable fix slide]</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/522d753f239f59c294d0388db94fd2349ed3741908a0726f81e20e12a9ca6611/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35663862313231616636636633373432656136643831653066316636616336342e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/522d753f239f59c294d0388db94fd2349ed3741908a0726f81e20e12a9ca6611/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35663862313231616636636633373432656136643831653066316636616336342e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.gyazo.com/5f8b121af6cf3742ea6d81e0f1f6ac64.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: you currently have access to calling the functions defined in a module even if you never evaluate it at all. In this proposal, that behavior would be removed, and you'd only get the functions if you really do it.</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: introducing new hypothetical API, need to define its semantics</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: The observable difference is about whether you encounter</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: This only happens from circularities</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: This is all about the interaction between circular dependencies between CJS and ESM</p>
<p dir="auto">YK: Why care if esm can or cannot see cjs</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: We want a single module system that can be used for ES</p>
<p dir="auto">I'm unable to type fast enough to keep up with this. Its hard to tease out the point when people start and stop statements mid-statement.</p>
<p dir="auto">I want to explain, I'm going to, Here's how I think we can explain, let me unpack (interrupted)</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: [suggesting some design where we "delay validation" of imports across module system boundaries]</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: That would be a big change; it's hard to understand what that would mean.</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: We may want to insert a lot more dynamism to solve this issue</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: How should ESM -&gt; CJS -&gt; ESM work?</p>
<p dir="auto">CP: you would have a couple stripes when crossing the boundary</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: That's why it's called zebra stripes</p>
<hr>
<p dir="auto">(break)</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Linking is very dynamic. The popular npm module "meow" relinks its parent. Used for CLI. When you require it, you get a new particular module per importer, which gives a modified version of it. We may need to revisit linking to support this.</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: What does this achieve?</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: This lets you tool out your CLI without knowing anything about your dependent. It lets your dependency learn about your module by reading its package.json.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: [Named imports slide] ESM cannot do named imports from CJS dependencies without mitigations. Our proposal is to hoist evaluation of the CJS module up to the linking phase.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/203c702677246e97d0d3e367a7afe298fe6eee5408427c0cfcee6eeb01fa54d3/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35386361373037363063333439643334666661373264313536653833623033322e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/203c702677246e97d0d3e367a7afe298fe6eee5408427c0cfcee6eeb01fa54d3/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35386361373037363063333439643334666661373264313536653833623033322e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.gyazo.com/58ca70760c349d34ffa72d156e83b032.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: No matter what we do, we will break Babel somehow, the question is just how.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: In our current proposal, we would take a snapshot of the exported properties of the object and export those names. We had considered more flexible behavior, but it seems unworkable.</p>
<p dir="auto">CP: How many people are using this?</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL, MRS: Some? It's unclear how many rely on it.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/792a49b7819c35e37c17828a7020e8c1789dc804284128a627f3188b6a549d39/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f61626635366164356639343061386638396231396539363032356535343862332e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/792a49b7819c35e37c17828a7020e8c1789dc804284128a627f3188b6a549d39/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f61626635366164356639343061386638396231396539363032356535343862332e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.gyazo.com/abf56ad5f940a8f89b19e96025e548b3.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: We could say that it just doesn't work properly if you import it as ES6.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Common on npm: "import {Component} from 'React'".</p>
<p dir="auto">ESM Doable needs</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">Context:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Remove existing "magic" variables</li>
<li>Built-in module like <code>import {url} from 'js:context'</code> to get these variables -- defer to iterate on details, relates to discussion in Portland</li>
<li>Early errors from non-existent context variables</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Hooks:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Need to ensure hookup prior to</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Some kind of loader spec, maintaining invariants of es262. May be related to the loader spec.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">----- Discussion
Context syntax details</p>
<p dir="auto">BT: There was earlier discussion about import.context which would be a grab-bag object for these things like these, championed by Dave Herman at the Portland 2015 TC39 meeting</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: If you want early errors, rather than getting undefined, then we could have <code>import.url</code> rather than <code>import.context.url</code> which would have an early error if you did <code>import.foobar</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: It is important for this to be host-extensible and not introduce desktop concepts to the web</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: Yes, there should be compatibility between Node and the Web, and we'd be open to trying to move away from Node-specific APIs.</p>
<p dir="auto">MSR: For extensibility, there are various cases, bundling loader, etc. These may hook into this in various ways.</p>
<p dir="auto">YK: I'm concerned about compatibility with <strong>filename</strong> and <strong>dirname</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Although the spec would allow it, we will not modify the absolute URLs. The main thing we would need is import.url; we may want another path for CJS metadata, but no other properties shared between environments.</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: I'm skeptical</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: dirname may be useful for a case where you have templates that you want to load from the directory where the JavaScript file is</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: This could be based on require.resolve within the Node ecosystem</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: In the loader spec work, there have been cases where import.url would not be such a clean thing to expose--for example, there could be two names that correspond to the same module.</p>
<p dir="auto">import.resolve is another proposal for a pseudofunction, taking a string literal or possibly a runtime string value, for resolving the absolute, rather than relative, path which gives a more canonicalized way to reach the module, which would also be a thing that could be passed into import.</p>
<p dir="auto">Generally: There is agreement in the room that getting the url and having a way to resolve an import into a url are important problems, and some subtle questions remaining about whether it should be a built-in module or pseudoproperty, as well as other details.</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: New interoperability linking suggestion: The validation to linking would not always be performed statically, but rather dynamically when hitting a CJS module, and in that case, deferring the invalidation until the beginning of the execution of the top-level ESM module body. The next part is, what does the dynamic validation look like. One option is, we preserve live bindings from CJS, and the other option is a snapshot. The latter option guarantees nothing disappearing, but this loses the aliasing semantics of ES6. This is all for the case of importing a CJS from ESM.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: There's a difference between snapshotting the list of property keys, and snapshotting the values of properties. I have proposed doing a live binding to the list of property keys which are available as one is exported from a CJS module after the initial evaluation, but to have bindings that are live from the CJS object to the module namespace object or direct usages</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: The Babel version does have some notion of live binding [because it translates named lookups to member expressions on the exports object]</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: e.g., used in Promisify.all. Changing the values is much more common than changing the keys.</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: Trying to pin things down. What is the specific evaluation order of an ESM module A importing from an ESM module B, and what exactly changes if B were a CJS module instead?</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: [described DH's previous proposal involving delaying resolving bindings imported from CJS into an ESM until after CJS evaluates during evaluation]. Example:</p>
<p dir="auto">// a
import {foo} from "b";
import {bar} from "c";</p>
<p dir="auto">// b
export let foo = 1;
console.log('hello');</p>
<p dir="auto">// c
console.log('world');
module.exports = { bar: 2 }</p>
<p dir="auto">Instantiation of a causes instantiation of b, but because c is a CJS module we defer its "instantation" till later (and in the meantime put the "bar" binding in a into TDZ)
Evaluation of a immediately causes b to evaluate (before evaluating any of the statements in a), then c to evaluate, and after c evaluates we can complete linking of a to c, thus initializing "bar" to 2. If c failed to export "bar", then an error would occur at this time (before any of a's statements execute).</p>
<p dir="auto">DH: Another possibility, more ambitious: We may be able to allow cycles, based on some reordering. Disallowing cycles would be an adoption hazard. The proposal here would require the earlier modules to fully resolve before the later modules come.</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: Tools can create cycles that didn't exist</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: How?</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: A downstream dependency may end up adding a dependency edge to something that uses it very indirectly, and a module in the middle of this cycle might not know about this but be affected</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: Cycles would not work with the idea I was describing before as requiring the ESM from the CJS that imports it would hang, as require is synchronous and wants a fully-formed answer immediately. Options include CP's making the namespace object partial, or returning a Promise, or Dave's changing the evaluation order.</p>
<p dir="auto">[AK: lots of discussion about a cyclical dependency graph involving CJS and ESM modules; q: how does evaluation order change? a: in several ways. q: do we know anything about the shape of the ESM modules themselves? a: not if there are StarExports that cross that boundary]</p>
<p dir="auto">Prohibit export* of a CJS module from an ESM module.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: We shouldn't return different shapes of modules at different times, e.g. if an ESM module imports a CJS module while CJS hasn't finished evaluating</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: We do support that in CJS right now, as a side-effect of how require works</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: It should be a dynamic error to try to import * from a CJS module if that module is in a purgatory state</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: Or we could relax the immutability of module namespace objects in a case where the imported-from module is dynamic. The immutability was mostly for optimizability.</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: Couldn't there also be security issues with allowing a namespace object to change after creation?</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: With everything being ESMs, we can do static resolution all the way down to the base binding. We can't necessarily do that when we have dynamic CJS modules in the middle there. We have to stop at that point. Seems like that requires a spec change. Ultimately, I think TDZs take care of it, but at present, in the ES spec, we assume that we can go all the way to the end, as opposed to going through multiple steps.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">11.3.a import()</h2><a id="user-content-113a-import" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 11.3.a import()" href="#113a-import"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">(Domenic Denicola)</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function">https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function</a></p>
<p dir="auto">DD: Presently, all module loading is done statically, top level. There are cases where you absolutely need to have conditional imports. There are many common use cases. Need to dynamically load a module, with a string. Returns a Promise for a module namespace object. The proposal keeps with out general stance of keeping proposals small; this is mostly syntax plus calling out to embedder hooks.</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: Does the occurrence of <code>import</code> turn the script into a module?</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: Initially, I thought to restrict it to modules, but no reason to restrict it.</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Many reasons to include for use in Node</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: Good way to bootstrap into modules</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: Why special form, not a function?</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: To give you a context</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: Want to be given a module specifier, e.g., for some embedders, a relative path which is resolved based on where you're calling this from.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function#an-actual-function">https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function#an-actual-function</a></p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function#a-new-binding-form">https://github.com/domenic/proposal-import-function#a-new-binding-form</a></p>
<p dir="auto">DD: This is better than inserting <code>&lt;script type=module&gt;</code> tags dynamically because it's based directly on module specifiers, easier to use, doesn't pollute DOM, etc. Not introducing a new binding form.</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: New embedder hook, HostFetchImportedModule (runtime equivalent of [[RequestedModules]])</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: <code>import(</code> is not currently legal, so there's no ambiguity with import declarations</p>
<p dir="auto">RW: Channeling DH from three years ago: <code>import(</code> creates confusion because it looks like a function but isn't a function.</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: This is a syntactic form that's function-like. super is a prominent one. Also, you can do (x =&gt; import(x))</p>
<p dir="auto">RW: That's a good precedent to cite for this (w/r to "it looks like a function, but isn't actually a function object")</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Promise.all([&quot;a&quot;, &quot;b&quot;].map(name =&gt; import(name)).then(() =&gt; ...)"><pre><span class="pl-v">Promise</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">all</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s">"a"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">"b"</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">map</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">name</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> ...<span class="pl-kos">)</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">BFS: To clarify, even in Node, it would return a Promise</p>
<p dir="auto">DD: Even if Node wants require to be synchronous, asynchronous background loading of modules is useful, e.g. lazily loading things from JSDOM.</p>
<p dir="auto">MRS: In Node, we'd probably still do sync I/O and just return a Promise</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Can still use require to <em>basically</em> this. The advantage to load the dep graph in a non-blocking way was explored via <code>require.async()</code> (pfft. whoops)</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: I was initially skeptical but like this proposal. Good for scripts, including for using built-in modules from scripts. Though you may want built-in modules to resolve synchronously.</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: But it may take a long time to load the built-in module and want it to be asynchronous</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: Also, we could add the import statement to scripts</p>
<p dir="auto">CP: Do you plan to allow require within module source text in Node?</p>
<p dir="auto">BFS: Probably we'll have some way to get ahold of require, but we'd really encourage people to use import.</p>
<p dir="auto">BB: Maybe you'd import require from a built-in module.</p>
<p dir="auto">AK: Why is there a new hook for HostFetchImportedModule?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: Isn't this like adding something to [[RequestedModules]] dynamically?</p>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">11.2.b Intl.Segmenter</h2><a id="user-content-112b-intlsegmenter" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 11.2.b Intl.Segmenter" href="#112b-intlsegmenter"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">(Daniel Ehrenberg)</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: Unicode defines breaking properties: grapheme, word, line, sentence breaks.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/d61a260d62c6d1ee8ca8bd22f7300146353ec4a1f87ece05fb3f3c59d5857894/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35376537376266363637366562613964653236666635326663663662646535662e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/d61a260d62c6d1ee8ca8bd22f7300146353ec4a1f87ece05fb3f3c59d5857894/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f35376537376266363637366562613964653236666635326663663662646535662e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.gyazo.com/57e77bf6676eba9de26ff52fcf6bde5f.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>

<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/5736b9b5c54170e93127932bf7f09461beba7ba39010c5e5152cfd0260148534/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f65323130333234313830663466643432366665393130346533663035383630382e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/5736b9b5c54170e93127932bf7f09461beba7ba39010c5e5152cfd0260148534/68747470733a2f2f692e6779617a6f2e636f6d2f65323130333234313830663466643432366665393130346533663035383630382e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.gyazo.com/e210324180f4fd426fe9104e3f058608.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Create a segmenter in your locale
let segmenter = Intl.Segmenter(&quot;fr&quot;, {type: &quot;word&quot;});

// Get an iterator over a string
let segmentIterator = segmenter.segment(&quot;Ceci n'est pas une pipe&quot;);

// Iterate over it!
for (let {index, breakType} of segmentIterator) {
  console.log(`index: ${index} breakType: ${breakType}`);
  break;
}"><pre><span class="pl-c">// Create a segmenter in your locale</span>
<span class="pl-k">let</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmenter</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Intl</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">Segmenter</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"fr"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-c1">type</span>: <span class="pl-s">"word"</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// Get an iterator over a string</span>
<span class="pl-k">let</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmenter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">segment</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Ceci n'est pas une pipe"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// Iterate over it!</span>
<span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">let</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>index<span class="pl-kos">,</span> breakType<span class="pl-kos">}</span> <span class="pl-k">of</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">`index: <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">${</span><span class="pl-s1">index</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> breakType: <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">${</span><span class="pl-s1">breakType</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>`</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">break</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Short-cut accelerated API:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="let segmentIterator = segmenter.segment(
&quot;Ceci n'est pas une pipe&quot;);

// next() returning undefined
segmentIterator.advance();

// index of current break result
segmentIterator.index();

// breakType of current break result
segmentIterator.breakType();"><pre><span class="pl-k">let</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">segmenter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">segment</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>
<span class="pl-s">"Ceci n'est pas une pipe"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// next() returning undefined</span>
<span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">advance</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// index of current break result</span>
<span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">index</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// breakType of current break result</span>
<span class="pl-s1">segmentIterator</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">breakType</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">WH: Is the iterator the only API you're proposing? If you just wanted to turn a string into an array of words in that string, is there a quick way of doing that?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: For now just planning on providing the lower-level API. Things like that can be built on top of it.</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: Only works if you have full ICU (<code>Intl.v8BreakIterator</code>), ideal if this can be made to work with small ICU</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: What does this do for indices at which there are no breaks? Does it have a concept of "no break", or does it just omit them from the iterator output?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: It omits them.</p>
<p dir="auto">WH:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Hello, &quot;world&quot;! \n\n"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Hello, "world"! \n\n
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Where do the word breaks go here, and are the decisions configurable?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: Explained in <a href="http://unicode.org/reports/tr29/" rel="nofollow">http://unicode.org/reports/tr29/</a> (UAX29)</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: Might be nice to also include a segmenter that indicates character boundaries; i.e., everywhere except between UTF16 surrogate pairs.</p>
<p dir="auto">AWB: Intl standard-optional, not standard-mandatory</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Is this functionality something that you want tied to the optionality?</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">BT: grapheme doesn't require a lot of data</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: The advice is: callout to ICU or you'll do it wrong</p>
<p dir="auto">BT: is Segmenter based on UAX29?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: Both UAX29 and UAX14</p>
<p dir="auto">Mixed discussion about ICU data, etc. Dan answers all questions.</p>
<p dir="auto">SYG: cannot reverse a string and get same breaks</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: Reversing doesn't make a difference. In either the forward or reverse case you may need arbitrarily long lookahead and lookbehind to determine the breaks. For example, there are emoji grapheme breaking rules that state that if you have an even number of characters preceding your position then you have a break, but if you have an odd number then you don't. So you need to consider the input string as a whole.</p>
<p dir="auto">WH: UAX29 lists lots of configuration sub-options for different kinds of breaking choices. Is it your intent to support those?</p>
<p dir="auto">DE: Yes.</p>
<p dir="auto">JSL: ideal to get rid of prefixed.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Conclusion/Resolution</h4><a id="user-content-conclusionresolution-2" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Conclusion/Resolution" href="#conclusionresolution-2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Stage 1 acceptance</li>
</ul>
